      "description": "Sohla makes a meal fit for a King - King Henry VIII to be exact. Prepare your stomachs for a lavish brunch, including all the works and more, in this episode of Ancient Recipes.\n\nTHE RECIPES\n \nPie Aloes of Beef Recipe:\n- For the aloes:\n- 1 boneless mutton leg\n- 1 bunch parsley, chopped\n- ¾ cup fresh thyme leaves, chopped\n- 6 large hard-boiled egg yolks\n- ⅓ cup raisins\n- ½ cup pitted and chopped dates\n- kosher salt\n \n1. Slice the mutton into thin slices. \n2. Saute parsley and thyme until wilted. \n3. Chop egg yolks. Combine with wilted herbs, raisins, dates, and season with salt. Divide this mixture in half. \n4. Spread half the egg yolk mixture onto the slices of mutton and roll them up. \n \nFor the crust & assembly:\n- 350 grams all purpose flour\n- ½ teaspoon kosher salt\n- 1 egg yolk\n- ¾ cup melted lard\n- hot water\n- sugar\n- ground cinnamon\n- saffron threads\n \n1. Whisk together the flour and salt. \n2. Add the egg yolk and lard and mix this together thoroughly. \n3. Add enough water to knead into a smooth dough. \n4. Flatten the dough into a circle about 17 inches wide. The thickness of the dough should be between ⅛ and ¼ inch. \n5. Arrange the aloes in the center of the pie crust in a circular shape, leaving enough space to fold the edges over like a galette. \n6. Sprinkle a little sugar, cinnamon, saffron & salt on top of the aloes. Top with the remaining egg mixture.\n7. Bring the edges of the pie crust up around the aloes so that it forms pleats and leaves a hole at the top.\n8. Bake at 375F until done.\n \nFor the syrup:\n- 1 slice white bread, toasted\n- 1 cup white wine\n- ¾ cup granulated sugar\n- 1 teaspoon ground cinnamon\n- 1 teaspoon ground ginger\n \n1. In a small pot, break up the bread and add wine, sugar, cinnamon, and ginger. \n2. Simmer until the sugar is dissolved and the bread is mushy. \n3. Strain. \n4. Pour the syrup through the hole at the top of the pie after it’s done baking & cooling.\n\nYpocras Jelly Recipe:\n- 2 calves feet\n- 1 veal shoulder\n- 1 gallon water\n- 1 gallon white wine\n- 2 teaspoons ground cinnamon \n- 1 teaspoon ground ginger\n- 2 cups granulated sugar\n- Dark blue/purple food coloring\n \n1. Add the calves’ feet, veal shoulder, water, and wine to a large pot. \n2. Cover and bring it to a boil. \n3. Reduce heat to a simmer, partially cover, and gently simmer for 6 hours. Skim off any skum that rises to the top.\n4. Strain and discard the solids. \n5. Add the cinnamon, ginger, and sugar to the mixture and mix well. \n6. Add some dark blue/purple food coloring.\n7. Portion into small glasses in the refrigerator to cool and solidify. \n\n#AncientRecipes\n\nSubscribe for more HISTORY:\nhttp://histv.co/SubscribeHistoryYT\n\nCheck out exclusive HISTORY content:\nHistory Newsletter - https://histv.co/newsletter\nWebsite - https://histv.co/History\nFacebook - https://histv.co/Facebook\nTwitter - https://histv.co/Twitter\n\nAncient Recipes with Sohla takes the food you know and love and traces it back to its origins.       "title": "Sohla Tries a (Vegan?!) Gladiator Grain Bowl | Ancient Recipes With Sohla",
      "description": "Check out Ancient Workouts with Omar, a new History Original coming to our YouTube channel on 1/8!\n\nTo welcome us into 2022, Sohla recreates a staple of the ancient gladiator diet, a chickpea and barley mash topped with fresh goats cheese. Learn more - and discover why gladiators actually had dad bods, in this episode of Ancient Recipes.\n\nTHE RECIPE\n\nPtisan Recipe\n- ⅓ cup dried chickpeas\n- ⅓ cup dried lentils\n- ⅓ cup dried peas\n- 1 cup unhulled barley \n- ½ cup olive oil\n- ½ bunch swiss chard, stemmed and finely chopped\n- 1 medium leek, finely chopped\n- ¾ cup finely chopped cilantro\n- ¾ cup finely chopped dill\n- 1 medium beet, peeled and finely chopped\n- ½ cup finely chopped mallows\n- 8 ounces cabbage sprouts\n- 2 teaspoons fennel seeds\n- 2 tablespoons fresh oregano leaves\n- ½ cup lightly packed lovage\n- Nuoc Mam to taste\n\n1. Rinse and soak the chickpeas, lentils, and peas overnight. Drain.\n2. Rinse the barley. In a molcajete, crush the barley until it’s broken down to a coarse meal. \n3. In a large saucepan, bring 2 quarts of water to a boil. Add the drained chickpeas, lentils, and peas, and the crushed barley. Simmer until totally tender and the texture of oatmeal.\n4. Meanwhile, boil the cabbage sprouts.\n5. Stir the olive oil into the barley porridge. Add the greens, leeks, cilantro, dill, beets, and mallows and cook until wilted.\n6. In a mortar & pestle, grind together the oregano, fennel seeds, lovage, and half the blanched sprouts. Add nuoc mam to taste. \n7. Chop up the remaining sprouts and set aside.\n8. Stir the with sprout puree into the porridge. \n9. Portion into bowls and garnish with the remaining chopped sprouts.\n\nStay up to date on all of your favorite The HISTORY Channel shows at http://history.com/schedule.\n\nAncient Recipes with Sohla takes the food you know and love and traces it back to its origins.       "title": "Sohla Cooks 3000-Year-Old Tamales for the Holidays | Ancient Recipes With Sohla",
      "description": "It's holiday season in the Ancient Recipes kitchen, so Sohla creates a holiday staple with truly ancient origins - tamales!\n\nTHE RECIPE\n\nMasa Dough Recipe:\n- 1 pound fresh masa\n- ½ teaspoon kosher salt\n- Dried corn husks\n\n1. Beat together fresh masa and kosher salt with 1 tablespoon of water at a time until spreadable. \n\nMayan Iguana Filling Recipe:\n- 4 dried guajillo chilies\n- 2 dried chipotle chilies\n- ½ pound tomatillos\n- 1 medium onion, peeled and cut into quarters\n- 1 pound boneless iguana meat\n- 1 tablespoon dried epazote\n- 1 ½ teaspoons kosher salt\n\n1. Use scissors to trim the stems off the guajillo and chipotles chilies and cut open. Remove the seeds. \n2. In a dry skillet or comal, toast the chiles until fragrant and darkened.\n3. Cover with warm water and soak at least 1 hour and up to overnight. \n4. In a dry skillet or comal over medium-high heat, char the tomatillos and onion until blackened all around. \n5. Add the tomatillos and onion to a molcajete or blender. Drain the chiles and add them in as well. Crush them all together in the molcajete adding water as you go to bring them together. Or if using a blender, add just enough water to cover and blend until smooth. \n6. In a medium saucepan or dutch oven, add the iguana meat, chili puree, epazote, salt, and enough water to almost cover the meat (add water if needed, the puree might be enough liquid). Cover and bring to a simmer.\n7. Reduce heat to maintain a gentle simmer, and cook uncovered until the iguana is tender. \n8. Using two forks, shred the iguana meat into small pieces. \n\nAztec Guava Filling Recipe:\n- 1 pound guavas, roughly chopped\n- 2 dried chipotle chilies\n- 1 teaspoon coriander seeds\n- One 3-inch cinnamon stick\n- ½ teaspoon kosher salt\n\n1. Combine the guavas, chipotles, coriander, cinnamon, and salt in medium saucepan and add enough water to come halfway up the fruit.\n2. Bring to a boil, then reduce heat to a simmer. Cook gently, breaking up the fruit with a wooden spoon, until the fruit is totally tender and jammy, about 1 hour. \n3. Pass the mixture through a colander or food mill to remove the seeds and spices.\n\nAssembling & cooking the tamales:\n- Corn husks\n\n1. Soak the corn husks overnight.\n2. Spread the masa evenly on the husk creating a thin layer.\n3. Add in a spoonful or two of either filling. \n4. Roll the tamale onto itself either in the traditional tamale shape or in the historical ball shape. Tie it together to keep its shape\n5. Place a layer of medium sized rocks at the bottom of a large stock pot. Add enough water to come up about halfway on the rocks.\n6. Place soaked corn husks on top of the rocks.\n7. Add the tamales on top of that, being careful not to have any filling spill out. \n8. Steam the tamales until the masa is tender and done\n\nStay up to date on all of your favorite The HISTORY Channel shows at http://history.com/schedule.\n\nAncient Recipes with Sohla takes the food you know and love and traces it back to its origins.       "publishedAt": "2021-12-03T15:59:23Z",
      "channelId": "UC9MAhZQQd9egwWCxrwSIsJQ",
      "title": "Who had the best Christmas cookie recipe? | Ancient Recipes With Sohla",
      "description": "What connects Abe Lincoln and Queen Elizabeth I? Gingerbread Men! Sohla explores two distinct but delicious recipes for these classic spiced cookies, in this holiday edition of Ancient Recipes.\n\nTHE RECIPES\n\nLincoln’s Gingerbread:\n- ⅔  cup whole milk\n- ⅔  cup sorghum syrup\n- 4 cups all-purpose flour\n- 2 tablespoons packed dark brown sugar\n- ½ teaspoon saleratus\n- 1 tablespoon ground dried ginger\n- ½ cup (1 stick) cold salted cultured butter, cut into cubes\n\n1. In a small bowl, mix together the milk and sorghum syrup. \n2. In a large bowl, whisk together the flour, sugar, saleratus, and ginger. Add the butter and cut into the flour until the mixture looks like a coarse cornmeal. \n3. Add the milk mixture into the flour mixture and mix well with a spoon. \n4. Heat oven to 325F. Break off a piece of dough a little larger than a golf ball. Place it on the work surface and roll it lightly under your palms to form a pencil-thin rope of dough about 12 inches long. \n5. Break off a 4-inch long piece and set aside. This will become the arms. \n6. Fold the remaining rope in half to form a narrow, upside down V. Grasp at the folded top, pinch together 1 inch down from the top and twist, forming the head and neck.\n7. Place the arm piece across the back and under the neck. Gently press to secure. Place on the prepared baking sheet. Repeat these steps with the remaining dough.\n8. Bake until the cookies are lightly browned, about 15 to 20 minutes. Watch closely as the sorghum or molasses in the dough tends to burn quickly.\n\nElizabeth I’s Gingerbread Recipe:\n- 3 loaves whole grain bread\n- ½ pound granulated sugar\n- ½ ounce ground cinnamon\n- ½ ounce ground dried ginger\n- ½ ounce ground dried licorice root\n- ½ ounce ground anise seeds\n- 1-quart white wine\n- water as needed\n\n1. Cube the bread and spread it out onto a sheet tray to stale for a few days. Grate the bread in batches until fine. Pass the crumbs through a coarse mesh sieve to sift away the bigger crumbs.\n2. In a large saucepan, mix together the sifted crumbs, cinnamon, ginger, licorice, and anise. Add the wine. Bring to a boil, and cook, stirring constantly, until you have a stiff paste. Add water as needed to achieve a paste consistency\n3. Transfer paste to a bowl to cool.\n4. Shape in the cookie molds & scrape off any excess.\n5. Arrange on a sheet tray, and bake at 350F until done. The time will depend on the size of the cookie molds.\n\n#AncientRecipes\n\nSubscribe for more Ancient Recipes with Sohla and other great The HISTORY Channel shows:\nhttp://histv.co/SubscribeHistoryYT\n\nLearn more about The HISTORY Channel and watch full episodes on our site:\nhttps://history.com\n\nCheck out exclusive HISTORY content:\nHistory Newsletter - https://histv.co/newsletter\nWebsite - https://histv.co/History\nFacebook - https://histv.co/Facebook\nTwitter - https://histv.co/Twitter\n\nStay up to date on all of your favorite The HISTORY Channel shows at http://history.com/schedule.\n\nAncient Recipes with Sohla takes the food you know and love and traces it back to its origins.       "channelId": "UC9MAhZQQd9egwWCxrwSIsJQ",
      "title": "Pemmican: The Original Survival Food | Ancient Recipes With Sohla",
      "description": "To celebrate Native American Heritage Month, Sohla recreates pemmican, a super food made of meat, fat and berries that dates back over 5,000 years. Plus Sohla speaks with indigenous chef Sean Sherman to learn more about the history of this remarkable dish, in this episode of Ancient Recipes with Sohla.\n\nTHE RECIPE\n\nIngredients:\n- 1 pound bison fat\n- 2 pounds lean, boneless bison \n- ⅔ cup dried chokeberries\n- 1 teaspoon kosher salt\n- ½ teaspoon freshly ground black pepper\n\n1. Cut the fat into 1-inch pieces and add to a medium saucepan.\n2. Trim any fat off the bison meat. Add the trimmed fat to the saucepan.\n3. Cook the fat over medium-low heat, stirring occasionally, until fully melted. Any bits of meat should be browned, rendered, and sunken to the bottom of the pot. This should take about 4 hours. \n4. Strain the rendered fat through a fine-mesh strainer and set aside. \n5. Add a cooling rack to a sheet pan. Thinly slice the bison and arrange on the cooling rack. Dehydrate at 160F until totally dry, about 12 hours. Cool completely before processing.\n6. Grind the dried meat into a powder using a mortar & pestle. Add the ground meat to a bowl.\n7. Grind the chokeberries in the mortar & pestle. Add it to the bowl with the ground meat.\n8. Add the melted bison fat, kosher salt, and maple sugar to the meat & berry mixture. Use your hands to mix everything until well combined.\n9. Take a handful of the mixture and shape into patties. Let rest for about 30 minutes.\n\n#AncientRecipes\n\nSubscribe for more Ancient Recipes with Sohla and other great The HISTORY Channel shows:\nhttp://histv.co/SubscribeHistoryYT\n\nLearn more about The HISTORY Channel and watch full episodes on our site:\nhttps://history.com\n\nCheck out exclusive HISTORY content:\nHistory Newsletter - https://histv.co/newsletter\nWebsite - https://histv.co/History\nFacebook - https://histv.co/Facebook\nTwitter - https://histv.co/Twitter\n\nStay up to date on all of your favorite The HISTORY Channel shows at http://history.com/schedule.\n\nAncient Recipes with Sohla takes the food you know and love and traces it back to its origins.
